# Inpainting - Recraft

> Documentation Index
> -------------------
> 
> Fetch the complete documentation index at: [/docs/llms.txt](https://www.recraft.ai/docs/llms.txt)
> 
> Use this file to discover all available pages before exploring further.

[Skip to main content](https://www.recraft.ai/docs/recraft-studio/frames/inpainting#content-area)

Inpainting lets you regenerate specific parts of an image while keeping the rest intact. This is useful for correcting details, replacing elements, or making creative changes without starting from scratch.

Inpainting is currently available in the old interface, which is accessible by clicking the **Old interface** toggle in the top navigation.

**How to use inpainting**:

1.  Select an image on the canvas.
2.  Click the **Edit area** button in the top toolbar.
3.  Choose a selection tool: **Lasso**, **Brush**, **Area**, or **Wand**.
4.  Highlight the part of the image you want to change.
5.  Enter a new prompt describing the desired update.
6.  Click the **generation button** to apply the edit. The selected area will be replaced based on your prompt while the rest of the image stays the same.

**Note**: When using inpainting on large images, Recraft automatically downscales the image before applying edits, which can result in a noticeable loss of quality in the final output.

[​](https://www.recraft.ai/docs/recraft-studio/frames/inpainting#tips-for-better-results)

Tips for better results
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

*   If the selected area is too small, the change may be subtle or unnoticeable. Select a larger area for more effective inpainting.
*   Inpainting works best on images resolutions of 1024 pixels or smaller. For larger images, Recraft automatically downscales before editing. The result will be returned at the supported resolution of 1024 pixels.
*   After multiple rounds of inpainting, image quality may begin to degrade. If that happens, try reverting to an earlier version and batch several edits together in a single step.
*   To learn more about the selection tools available, visit [Selection tools](https://www.recraft.ai/docs/recraft-studio/work-area/selection-tools)
    .

[Introduction to frames](https://www.recraft.ai/docs/recraft-studio/frames/introduction-to-frames)
[Outpainting](https://www.recraft.ai/docs/recraft-studio/frames/outpainting)

⌘I

Assistant

Responses are generated using AI and may contain mistakes.

# History - Recraft

> Documentation Index
> -------------------
> 
> Fetch the complete documentation index at: [/docs/llms.txt](https://www.recraft.ai/docs/llms.txt)
> 
> Use this file to discover all available pages before exploring further.

[Skip to main content](https://www.recraft.ai/docs/recraft-studio/history#content-area)

All images you generate, including images from deleted projects, appear in both the **History page** and the **History panel**. You can access History in two ways:

*   From the **Recraft home menu** in the top navigation, select **History** to open the full [History page](https://www.recraft.ai/history)
    .
*   From within a project, click **History** in the top navigation to open the History panel.

### 

[​](https://www.recraft.ai/docs/recraft-studio/history#history-page)

History page

The **History page** is the primary place to manage your generated images. It provides full functionality, including:

*   filtering by type
*   searching across your entire history
*   viewing detailed image metadata
*   copying prompts and image links
*   downloading images
*   deleting images (under premium plans)
*   selecting multiple images for bulk actions

Use the History page when you need to review, organize, or clean up your image history.

### 

[​](https://www.recraft.ai/docs/recraft-studio/history#history-panel)

History panel

The **History panel** opens inside a project and is designed for quick access and reuse. It supports:

*   filtering by type
*   searching your image history
*   viewing detailed image metadata
*   copying prompts and image links
*   downloading images
*   dragging images onto the canvas
*   inserting a copy of an image into the current project
*   deleting images (under premium plans)

The History panel displays generations in a grid of square tiles. You can filter the content by **Image** or **Video** to quickly find specific generations. The same filtering options are available in the **History panel on Canvas**. Generations are grouped by date, making it easier to browse creations from specific days.

[​](https://www.recraft.ai/docs/recraft-studio/history#browsing-and-searching-history-page)

Browsing and searching (History page)
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

### 

[​](https://www.recraft.ai/docs/recraft-studio/history#filters)

Filters

You can filter items on the History page using the **Type** filter to display either **Images** or **Videos**. You can also view your history grouped by date for easier navigation.

### 

[​](https://www.recraft.ai/docs/recraft-studio/history#search)

Search

Use the search bar to find images using simple keywords, such as _red panda_ or _rainbow cake_.  
Search matches against the prompt used to generate the image.

[​](https://www.recraft.ai/docs/recraft-studio/history#working-with-images-history-page)

Working with images (History page)
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

### 

[​](https://www.recraft.ai/docs/recraft-studio/history#hover-actions)

Hover actions

When you hover over an image thumbnail, you can:

*   Copy the prompt
*   Download the image
*   Delete the image (under premium plans)
*   Select the image for bulk actions (a checkbox appears in the corner)

### 

[​](https://www.recraft.ai/docs/recraft-studio/history#image-detail-panel)

Image detail panel

Click any image to open its image detail panel. This panel shows:

*   the prompt used to generate the image
*   whether the image is raster or vector
*   the aspect ratio
*   the model or style used

From the image detail panel, you can also:

*   add the image to Favorites
*   copy the image URL
*   download the image
*   permanently delete the image (under premium plans)

[​](https://www.recraft.ai/docs/recraft-studio/history#bulk-actions-on-images-history-page)

Bulk actions on images (History page)
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Bulk selection allows you to perform actions on multiple images at once.

### 

[​](https://www.recraft.ai/docs/recraft-studio/history#selecting-multiple-images)

Selecting multiple images

1.  Open the [History](https://www.recraft.ai/history)
     page.
2.  Hover over a thumbnail to reveal the checkbox in the corner.
3.  Click the checkbox to select the image.
4.  Continue selecting additional images as needed.
    *   A bulk action bar appears at the bottom showing how many images are selected.
5.  Click a checkbox again to deselect an image.
6.  Click the **X** in the bulk action bar to clear all selections.

### 

[​](https://www.recraft.ai/docs/recraft-studio/history#bulk-delete-download-or-favorite)

Bulk delete, download, or favorite

Once one or more images are selected, the bulk action bar lets you:

*   **Download** all selected images
*   **Favorite** all selected images
*   **Delete** all selected images (confirmation required)

**Note**: Bulk delete cannot be undone. You can still regenerate images later using their original prompts.

[​](https://www.recraft.ai/docs/recraft-studio/history#using-images-in-your-canvas)

Using images in your canvas
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

From the **History panel** inside a project:

*   Drag an image onto the canvas to place it directly
*   Or click a thumbnail to insert a copy into your current project

Images added from History behave like any other canvas image and can be edited, transformed, or combined with other elements.

[Recoloring existing images](https://www.recraft.ai/docs/recraft-studio/color-palettes/recoloring-existing-images)
[Favorites](https://www.recraft.ai/docs/recraft-studio/libraries/favorites)

⌘I

Assistant

Responses are generated using AI and may contain mistakes.

# Quick start - Recraft

> Documentation Index
> -------------------
> 
> Fetch the complete documentation index at: [/docs/llms.txt](https://www.recraft.ai/docs/llms.txt)
> 
> Use this file to discover all available pages before exploring further.

[Skip to main content](https://www.recraft.ai/docs/recraft-studio/quick-start#content-area)

This quick start guide walks you through the core steps to begin creating images in Recraft Studio. You’ll create an account, generate your first image, make a simple edit, and export the result.

1

[](https://www.recraft.ai/docs/recraft-studio/quick-start#)

Create a Recraft account
------------------------

Go to recraft.ai and click [Start now free](https://www.recraft.ai/auth/login?callbackUrl=%2F)
. Choose one of the available sign-in methods:

*   Email
*   Google
*   Discord
*   Apple

No password is required. If you sign up with email, you’ll receive a one-time code to complete sign-in.New accounts include free credits so you can start generating images right away.If you already have an account, you can skip this step.

2

[](https://www.recraft.ai/docs/recraft-studio/quick-start#)

Create a new project
--------------------

Open [Recraft Studio](https://www.recraft.ai/)
 from your browser. If prompted, sign in to continue.You’ll land on the Projects view, where all your work is organized.From here, click **Create new project** to open an empty canvas.

3

[](https://www.recraft.ai/docs/recraft-studio/quick-start#)

Generate your first image
-------------------------

At the bottom of the canvas, use the prompt panel to describe what you want to generate, then click the arrow button to generate.After a few seconds, your image will appear on the canvas in a bounding box.(Optional) Adjust settings such as model, style, aspect ratio, or image count.

4

[](https://www.recraft.ai/docs/recraft-studio/quick-start#)

Make your first edit
--------------------

Select the image on the canvas to reveal editing options.You can make simple changes using tools like natural language editing, background removal, or area selection.Edits create a new version of the image while keeping the original intact.

5

[](https://www.recraft.ai/docs/recraft-studio/quick-start#)

Export your image
-----------------

When you’re happy with the result, export the image from the canvas.Select the image and click **Export** in the upper right or right-click the image and select **Export as…**Choose a format such as PNG, JPG, PDF, and TIFF for raster images; or SVG, PDF, and Lottie for vector images.

[​](https://www.recraft.ai/docs/recraft-studio/quick-start#what%E2%80%99s-next)

What’s next
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

From here, you can explore [styles](https://www.recraft.ai/docs/recraft-studio/styles/overview)
, create vectors, generate [mockups](https://www.recraft.ai/docs/recraft-studio/mockups/how-to-create-a-mockup)
, or work with more advanced editing tools.

[Overview](https://www.recraft.ai/docs/recraft-studio/overview)
[Interface overview](https://www.recraft.ai/docs/recraft-studio/interface-overview)

⌘I

Assistant

Responses are generated using AI and may contain mistakes.

# How to import an image - Recraft

> Documentation Index
> -------------------
> 
> Fetch the complete documentation index at: [/docs/llms.txt](https://www.recraft.ai/docs/llms.txt)
> 
> Use this file to discover all available pages before exploring further.

[Skip to main content](https://www.recraft.ai/docs/recraft-studio/importing/how-to-import-an-image#content-area)

There are a few ways to import an image:

*   Drag and drop an image directly from your system file browser onto the canvas
*   Click the **Upload image** button in the **toolbar**
*   Click **History** in the top navigation to open the history panel. Click on any image to place it onto the canvas.

Once placed, an imported image will behave like any other canvas element. You can resize, rotate, and reposition it as needed. **Note**: Imported images are not used for training AI models.

[About importing](https://www.recraft.ai/docs/recraft-studio/importing/about-importing)
[Size limits and supported formats of imported images](https://www.recraft.ai/docs/recraft-studio/importing/size-limits-and-supported-formats)

# Teams overview - Recraft

> Documentation Index
> -------------------
> 
> Fetch the complete documentation index at: [/docs/llms.txt](https://www.recraft.ai/docs/llms.txt)
> 
> Use this file to discover all available pages before exploring further.

[Skip to main content](https://www.recraft.ai/docs/teams/teams-overview#content-area)

The Teams plan is designed for organizations that need a shared creative environment with centralized credit usage and administrative control. This plan activates a **Workspace**, which serves as a collaborative space for team members to generate, edit, and manage assets together. A workspace:

*   Requires a minimum of 3 seats
*   Allows any member to be assigned the **Admin** role to invite or remove members, manage seat count, and handle billing
*   Provides a set number of monthly credits (2,000, 4,000, 8,000, or 16,000, depending on the selected credit plan) for each workspace member.
*   Includes access to first-priority customer support

**Note**: Monthly credits are not sharable between members. Each workspace member occupies a seat and receives full access to all paid subscription features and benefits:

*   Generated images are private
*   Commercial license: full ownership and usage rights for all generations made under the paid plan
*   Unlimited image uploads (vs. 3/day on Free)
*   Priority image generation
*   Maximum concurrent jobs: 10
*   Maximum images per prompt: 4
*   Access to external models
*   Artistic level control
*   Ability to extract detailed and optimized image prompts
*   Custom color palette input
*   Magic wand tool for enhanced selection and edits
*   Access to the Creative Upscale tool

If the workspace subscription ends or becomes inactive, all members revert to individual Free or Basic plan access, depending on their previous plan. Unused prepaid fees are not refunded. **Note**: Imported images, whether added to the canvas or uploaded to create a custom style, are not used for training AI models.

[Commercial rights and ownership](https://www.recraft.ai/docs/plans-and-billing/commercial-rights-and-ownership)
[Teams workspace admin page](https://www.recraft.ai/docs/teams/teams-workspace-admin)

⌘I

Assistant

Responses are generated using AI and may contain mistakes.

# About importing - Recraft

> Documentation Index
> -------------------
> 
> Fetch the complete documentation index at: [/docs/llms.txt](https://www.recraft.ai/docs/llms.txt)
> 
> Use this file to discover all available pages before exploring further.

[Skip to main content](https://www.recraft.ai/docs/recraft-studio/importing/about-importing#content-area)

Recraft Studio lets you bring your own images into the canvas. Imported images can be used across the platform’s tools, from mockups and vectorization to prompt-based editing and fine-tuning. Once imported, your image can be used to:

*   Generate a variation of the original visual
*   Use as a reference for prompt-based generation
*   Remove the background
*   Vectorize raster images (e.g., PNG to SVG)
*   Remix or edit specific areas with prompts
*   Apply your image to a product mockup
*   Extend the image using outpainting (frame tool)
*   Create a custom style for consistent generation
*   Upscale to increase resolution and detail

**Notes on imported and edited images**

*   Only **original generated images** are saved to project history. Images that have been edited e.g., background removed or fine-tuned) will not appear in the project timeline.
*   Imported images, whether added to the canvas or uploaded to create a custom style, are not used for training AI models.
*   To reuse edited images, first **export them**, then **re-import** as needed.
*   When importing an image, Recraft Studio may default to an external model to enable natural language editing.

[Background tools](https://www.recraft.ai/docs/recraft-studio/image-editing/background-tools)
[How to import an image](https://www.recraft.ai/docs/recraft-studio/importing/how-to-import-an-image)

⌘I

Assistant

Responses are generated using AI and may contain mistakes.

# Size limits and supported formats of imported images - Recraft

> Documentation Index
> -------------------
> 
> Fetch the complete documentation index at: [/docs/llms.txt](https://www.recraft.ai/docs/llms.txt)
> 
> Use this file to discover all available pages before exploring further.

[Skip to main content](https://www.recraft.ai/docs/recraft-studio/importing/size-limits-and-supported-formats#content-area)

JPG, PNG, WebP:

*   Width and height dimensions should not exceed 5800 pixels each
*   Max resolution: 16 megapixels
*   Max file size: 48MB

SVG:

*   Max file size: 48MB

# Teams workspace admin page - Recraft

> Documentation Index
> -------------------
> 
> Fetch the complete documentation index at: [/docs/llms.txt](https://www.recraft.ai/docs/llms.txt)
> 
> Use this file to discover all available pages before exploring further.

[Skip to main content](https://www.recraft.ai/docs/teams/teams-workspace-admin#content-area)

The **Teams workspace admin page** is where Team plan administrators manage their organization’s workspace. From here, admins can update company information, control seat usage, invite or remove members, and handle subscription settings. This dashboard is available only to users with **Admin** permissions in a Team workspace.

[​](https://www.recraft.ai/docs/teams/teams-workspace-admin#what-you-can-do-in-the-teams-workspace-admin-page)

What you can do in the Teams workspace admin page
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

### 

[​](https://www.recraft.ai/docs/teams/teams-workspace-admin#manage-seats)

Manage seats

Admins can adjust how many people are part of the workspace.

*   **Buy more seats**: Increase the number of available seats as your team grows.
*   **View total seats**: See your current seat count and how many are filled.
*   **Invite members**: Add new users by email.
*   **Remove members**: Free up a seat by removing someone from the workspace.

### 

[​](https://www.recraft.ai/docs/teams/teams-workspace-admin#assign-roles-and-permissions)

Assign roles and permissions

Each person in the workspace can be assigned a role. Roles determine what they can access or manage inside Recraft.

*   **Admin**: Full workspace control, including inviting and removing members, updating company information, managing seats, and accessing subscription settings.
*   **Member**: Can use Recraft with all paid features but cannot make workspace-level changes.

You can change a user’s role at any time using the dropdown next to their name.

### 

[​](https://www.recraft.ai/docs/teams/teams-workspace-admin#update-workspace-details)

Update workspace details

Workspace identity and billing information can be managed directly in the dashboard.

*   **Company name**
*   **Billing name**
*   **Billing email**
*   **Workspace avatar/logo**

Changes apply immediately across the workspace and will appear on invoices and subscription records.

### 

[​](https://www.recraft.ai/docs/teams/teams-workspace-admin#manage-your-subscription)

Manage your subscription

The dashboard provides direct access to plan and billing controls.

*   **Manage subscription**: Opens the subscription panel within Stripe, where you can view your current plan, update payment methods, switch plans, or cancel your subscription.
*   **Next invoice date**: Shows when your workspace subscription will renew.

Subscription management is handled through the desktop version of Recraft.

### 

[​](https://www.recraft.ai/docs/teams/teams-workspace-admin#view-people-and-credit-balance)

View people and credit balance

Under **People**, each workspace member shows:

*   **Email**
*   **Credits left** (each seat receives the monthly 9,000-credit allowance from the Team plan)
*   **Role**

The credit pool is shared across the workspace, but each member sees their own remaining balance.

### 

[​](https://www.recraft.ai/docs/teams/teams-workspace-admin#danger-zone)

Danger zone

Workspace admins can delete the entire workspace. **Delete workspace**: Permanently removes the workspace and all associated data. This action cannot be undone. _(Deleting the workspace does not affect your personal Recraft account.)_

[​](https://www.recraft.ai/docs/teams/teams-workspace-admin#when-to-use-the-teams-workspace-admin-page)

When to use the Teams workspace admin page
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Use this dashboard whenever you need to:

*   Add new members to your team
*   Remove someone who no longer needs access
*   Increase or reduce your total seat count
*   Update billing details before your next invoice
*   Change who has admin permissions
*   Adjust your subscription or review renewal dates
*   Rebrand your workspace with the correct name or logo

[Teams overview](https://www.recraft.ai/docs/teams/teams-overview)

⌘I

Assistant

Responses are generated using AI and may contain mistakes.

# Applying your design to the mockup - Recraft

> Documentation Index
> -------------------
> 
> Fetch the complete documentation index at: [/docs/llms.txt](https://www.recraft.ai/docs/llms.txt)
> 
> Use this file to discover all available pages before exploring further.

[Skip to main content](https://www.recraft.ai/docs/recraft-studio/mockups/applying-your-design-to-a-mockup#content-area)

Once the mockup frame is ready, you can add and position your artwork:

1.  Upload or generate your design (image, logo, text, etc.) onto the canvas.
2.  Place it over the mockup frame.
3.  Adjust **position**, **size**, and **rotation**.
4.  Use available styling options:
    *   **Appearance settings**: Control blending, texture, shading, and how the design interacts with the surface.
    *   **Tiling**: Repeat the design pattern across the mockup.
    *   **Masking**: Limit where the design appears on the mockup surface.
5.  When you’re satisfied, select the mockup image and export it as a PNG, JPG, PDF, or TIFF (CMYK) format.

[​](https://www.recraft.ai/docs/recraft-studio/mockups/applying-your-design-to-a-mockup#appearance-settings)

Appearance settings
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

The Appearance panel controls how the applied design visually interacts with the mockup surface. These settings affect only the design layer, not the mockup base.

### 

[​](https://www.recraft.ai/docs/recraft-studio/mockups/applying-your-design-to-a-mockup#blend-mode)

Blend mode

Blend mode determines how the colors and brightness of the design combine with the underlying mockup.

| Blend mode | Description |
| --- | --- |
| **Normal** | Displays the design as-is, without blending with the mockup colors. |
| **Darken** | Keeps the darker pixels from either the design or the mockup, allowing lighter areas to drop out. |
| **Multiply** | Darkens the result by combining design and mockup colors, making the design appear printed into shadows. |
| **Color Burn** | Deepens shadows and increases contrast by darkening the mockup based on the design. |
| **Lighten** | Keeps the lighter pixels from either the design or the mockup, removing darker design areas. |
| **Screen** | Brightens the result by lightening darker areas while preserving highlights. |
| **Color Dodge** | Intensifies highlights by brightening the mockup using the design’s lighter colors. |
| **Overlay** | Increases contrast by darkening shadows and lightening highlights while preserving midtones. |
| **Soft Light** | Applies a subtle contrast adjustment, gently lightening or darkening based on the design. |
| **Hard Light** | Applies strong contrast, similar to Overlay but with a more pronounced effect. |
| **Difference** | Produces an inverted, high-contrast result by subtracting color values between layers. |
| **Exclusion** | Similar to Difference but with lower contrast and softer color inversion. |
| **Hue** | Applies the design’s hue while preserving the mockup’s brightness and saturation. |
| **Saturation** | Applies the design’s saturation while preserving the mockup’s hue and brightness. |
| **Color** | Applies the design’s hue and saturation while preserving the mockup’s brightness. |
| **Luminosity** | Applies the design’s brightness while preserving the mockup’s color information. |

### 

[​](https://www.recraft.ai/docs/recraft-studio/mockups/applying-your-design-to-a-mockup#ai-blend-mode)

AI Blend mode

AI Blend mode applies adaptive, AI-generated shading to the design based on the lighting, folds, and contours of the mockup surface. When enabled, the design appears more naturally integrated into the product. AI Blend mode works alongside standard blend modes and can be toggled on or off independently.

### 

[​](https://www.recraft.ai/docs/recraft-studio/mockups/applying-your-design-to-a-mockup#show-texture)

Show texture

Show texture controls whether the surface texture of the mockup is applied to the design.

*   **Yes**: The design inherits surface details such as fabric grain or material texture.
*   **No**: The design appears smooth and uniform on the surface.

This setting affects texture only and does not change lighting or shading.

### 

[​](https://www.recraft.ai/docs/recraft-studio/mockups/applying-your-design-to-a-mockup#tiling)

Tiling

Tiling controls how the design repeats across the mockup surface.

*   **None**: The design appears once.
*   **Repeat**: The design is tiled evenly across the surface.
*   **Mirror**: The design is tiled with alternating mirrored tiles to reduce visible seams.

Tiling works best with seamless patterns.

### 

[​](https://www.recraft.ai/docs/recraft-studio/mockups/applying-your-design-to-a-mockup#masking-the-design)

Masking the design

Masking lets you hide or reveal parts of a design so it fits the surface of a mockup, such as fabric folds, edges, or object contours. To edit a mask:

1.  Select the design placed on top of the mockup.
2.  Open **Edit mask** in the right sidebar.
3.  Choose a **Selection** mode:
    *   **Brush**: Paint freeform areas into the mask.
    *   **Lasso**: Draw a closed shape to define a masked region.
    *   **Area**: Select a rectangular region to add to the mask.
    *   **Wand**: Automatically selects contiguous areas based on visual boundaries.
4.  Set **Show mask → Yes** to visualize the active mask while editing.

#### 

[​](https://www.recraft.ai/docs/recraft-studio/mockups/applying-your-design-to-a-mockup#precision-controls)

Precision controls

*   When using the **Brush** tool, hold **Shift** while dragging to constrain the stroke to a straight line.
*   You can also hold **Shift** and click to continue the previous brush stroke in a straight line. This is useful for outlining rigid or angled edges, such as a rotated rectangle.

#### 

[​](https://www.recraft.ai/docs/recraft-studio/mockups/applying-your-design-to-a-mockup#erasing-parts-of-a-mask)

Erasing parts of a mask

*   Hold **Option** (Alt) while using **Brush**, **Lasso**, or **Area** to erase parts of the existing mask.
*   This allows you to quickly correct mistakes, such as removing unwanted cutouts where parts of the design disappear.

#### 

[​](https://www.recraft.ai/docs/recraft-studio/mockups/applying-your-design-to-a-mockup#brush-size)

Brush size

*   When **Brush** is selected, adjust **Brush size** using the slider in the **Edit mask** panel for finer or broader control.

When finished, close **Edit mask** or toggle **Show mask → No** to return to the normal canvas view.

[How to create a mockup](https://www.recraft.ai/docs/recraft-studio/mockups/how-to-create-a-mockup)
[Using color palettes in generation](https://www.recraft.ai/docs/recraft-studio/color-palettes/using-color-palettes-in-generation)

⌘I

Assistant

Responses are generated using AI and may contain mistakes.

# Favorites - Recraft

> Documentation Index
> -------------------
> 
> Fetch the complete documentation index at: [/docs/llms.txt](https://www.recraft.ai/docs/llms.txt)
> 
> Use this file to discover all available pages before exploring further.

[Skip to main content](https://www.recraft.ai/docs/recraft-studio/libraries/favorites#content-area)

Favorites is a personal library for saving and revisiting images you want quick access to later. It allows you to collect useful, inspiring, or frequently reused images in one place, independent of any single project. Favorites is part of **Libraries**. It exists outside the canvas and persists across projects and sessions.

[​](https://www.recraft.ai/docs/recraft-studio/libraries/favorites#what-favorites-is-for)

What Favorites is for
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Favorites is designed to help you:

*   save images you want to reuse or reference later
*   keep important or high-quality generations easy to find
*   collect inspiration without duplicating or exporting files
*   access saved images across different projects

Favoriting an image does not change the image itself or affect the project it belongs to.

[​](https://www.recraft.ai/docs/recraft-studio/libraries/favorites#adding-images-to-favorites)

Adding images to Favorites
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

There are three ways to add an image to Favorites:

*   From the canvas, right-click an image and select **Add to Favorites**
*   From **History**, hover over an image and click the **heart icon**
*   From **Community**, hover over an image and click the **heart icon**

When an image is favorited, the **red heart icon** appears filled. Favorited images are saved to your Favorites library for easy access and reuse.

[​](https://www.recraft.ai/docs/recraft-studio/libraries/favorites#accessing-favorites)

Accessing Favorites
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Favorites can be accessed in two ways:

*   Click the **Recraft (R) icon** in the top navigation and select **Favorites**
*   Open the [Favorites page](https://www.recraft.ai/liked)
     directly

Favorites opens as a standalone library view outside the canvas.

[​](https://www.recraft.ai/docs/recraft-studio/libraries/favorites#actions-available-on-favorites)

Actions available on Favorites
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Favorites supports two interaction levels: **hover actions** for quick access, and **image detail actions** when you open an image.

### 

[​](https://www.recraft.ai/docs/recraft-studio/libraries/favorites#on-hover)

On hover

When you hover over an image in Favorites, you can:

*   **Copy prompt**: Copy the prompt used to generate the image
*   **Download**: Download the image to your device
*   **Remove from Favorites**: Click the **heart icon** to remove the image from Favorites

### 

[​](https://www.recraft.ai/docs/recraft-studio/libraries/favorites#on-click-image-detail-view)

On click (image detail view)

When you click an image, an image detail panel opens. From there, you can:

*   **View metadata**: See details such as model, style, image type (raster or vector), and aspect ratio
*   **View prompt**: Inspect the full prompt used to generate the image
*   **Copy link**: Copy a direct link to the image
*   **Download**: Download the image
*   **Remove from Favorites**: Remove the image from Favorites

These actions do not modify the original image or the project it came from.

[​](https://www.recraft.ai/docs/recraft-studio/libraries/favorites#removing-images-from-favorites)

Removing images from Favorites
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Removing an image from Favorites does not delete the image or affect its original location. To remove an image from Favorites:

*   Open **Favorites**
*   Hover over the image and click the **heart icon** to remove it from Favorites

[History](https://www.recraft.ai/docs/recraft-studio/history)
[Community](https://www.recraft.ai/docs/recraft-studio/libraries/community)

⌘I

Assistant

Responses are generated using AI and may contain mistakes.

# Community - Recraft

> Documentation Index
> -------------------
> 
> Fetch the complete documentation index at: [/docs/llms.txt](https://www.recraft.ai/docs/llms.txt)
> 
> Use this file to discover all available pages before exploring further.

[Skip to main content](https://www.recraft.ai/docs/recraft-studio/libraries/community#content-area)

Community is a public inspiration library that showcases images created with Recraft. It is designed for exploration, discovery, and learning. Community is part of **Libraries** and exists outside the canvas. Browsing Community does not affect your current project or selection.

[​](https://www.recraft.ai/docs/recraft-studio/libraries/community#what-community-is-for)

What Community is for
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Community is intended to help you:

*   explore what others are creating with Recraft
*   discover visual styles, compositions, and prompt ideas
*   find inspiration for new projects or directions
*   learn how different models and styles behave in practice

Community is not a workspace and does not store your personal assets.

[​](https://www.recraft.ai/docs/recraft-studio/libraries/community#accessing-community)

Accessing Community
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

You can open Community at any time:

*   Click the **Recraft (R) icon** in the top navigation and select **Community**, or go directly to [Community](https://www.recraft.ai/community)
    

Opening Community does not interrupt your current work. You can return to the canvas at any time.

[​](https://www.recraft.ai/docs/recraft-studio/libraries/community#browsing-community)

Browsing Community
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Community displays a curated feed of public images generated with Recraft. When browsing Community, you can:

*   scroll through images to explore different visual approaches
*   hover over an image to reveal quick actions
*   click an image to open a context panel with more details
*   inspect prompts and generation settings when available

When hovering over an image, you can click the **heart icon** to save it to [Favorites](https://www.recraft.ai/docs/recraft-studio/libraries/favorites)
. A filled heart (shown as a red heart) indicates the image has been favorited. Clicking an image opens a context panel where you can view additional information such as the prompt, model, format, and aspect ratio, and access available actions like copying a link or downloading the image. Community includes filtering options to help narrow what you see. You can filter images by type, including:

*   All images
*   Photorealism
*   Illustration
*   Vector art
*   Icon

Community content is read-only. Images cannot be edited directly in place.

[​](https://www.recraft.ai/docs/recraft-studio/libraries/community#using-community-images)

Using Community images
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Community images are provided for reference and inspiration. You can:

*   view prompts and settings to understand how an image was created
*   download an image and import it into your canvas to use as a reference image
*   use Community images as visual inspiration for your own prompts

Community images are not added to your projects automatically. To work with an image in your own project, recreate it using its prompt, or download and import it as a reference image before generating new content.

[Favorites](https://www.recraft.ai/docs/recraft-studio/libraries/favorites)
[Templates](https://www.recraft.ai/docs/recraft-studio/templates)

⌘I

Assistant

Responses are generated using AI and may contain mistakes.

# How to create a mockup - Recraft

> Documentation Index
> -------------------
> 
> Fetch the complete documentation index at: [/docs/llms.txt](https://www.recraft.ai/docs/llms.txt)
> 
> Use this file to discover all available pages before exploring further.

[Skip to main content](https://www.recraft.ai/docs/recraft-studio/mockups/how-to-create-a-mockup#content-area)

Mockups allow you to place your artwork, logo, or design onto product photography, such as T-shirts, tote bags, cups, or packaging, directly within the Recraft canvas. You can either generate a mockup from scratch or convert an existing image into a mockup frame.

[​](https://www.recraft.ai/docs/recraft-studio/mockups/how-to-create-a-mockup#mockup-collections)

Mockup collections
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Click the **Mockup** icon in the toolbar to open the mockup panel. From there you can:

*   Browse four collections of pre-made mockups: **Apparel**, **Packaging**, **Devices**, and **Outdoor ads**
*   Upload a mockup from your computer
*   Generate a mockup from scratch

The same four collections are also accessible via the **Get started** window. Select any ready-made mockup from a collection to add it directly to the canvas.

#### 

[​](https://www.recraft.ai/docs/recraft-studio/mockups/how-to-create-a-mockup#there-are-three-ways-to-create-a-mockup)

There are three ways to create a mockup:

#### 

[​](https://www.recraft.ai/docs/recraft-studio/mockups/how-to-create-a-mockup#1-use-a-pre-made-mockup-from-a-collection)

1\. Use a pre-made mockup from a collection

1.  Click the **Mockup** icon in the toolbar to open the panel.
2.  Browse the collections and select a mockup to add to the canvas.
3.  Apply your design following the steps in [Applying your design to the mockup](https://www.recraft.ai/docs/recraft-studio/mockups/applying-your-design-to-a-mockup)
    .

![Screenshot 2026 06 04 At 02 00 13](https://mintcdn.com/recraft/6-u2sHdMmgyc5RJE/images/Screenshot-2026-06-04-at-02.00.13.png?w=2500&fit=max&auto=format&n=6-u2sHdMmgyc5RJE&q=85&s=b901358d726eb2e2b3d2d0263dd03e65)

#### 

[​](https://www.recraft.ai/docs/recraft-studio/mockups/how-to-create-a-mockup#2-generate-a-mockup-from-scratch)

2\. Generate a mockup from scratch

Use this option if you want to start from a prompt:

1.  Open the prompt panel and select **Mockup** as the generation type (where you switch between Image / Video / etc.).
2.  Write a prompt describing the product you want to visualize (e.g., “white T-shirt facing forward”).
3.  Press **Enter** or click the **up arrow** to generate a mockup-ready image.

Once generated, the image is automatically converted into a mockup frame.

![Screenshot 2026 06 04 At 01 56 54](https://mintcdn.com/recraft/97KIOk2t0_rKrhao/images/Screenshot-2026-06-04-at-01.56.54.png?w=2500&fit=max&auto=format&n=97KIOk2t0_rKrhao&q=85&s=440dc46b2a30c667bf091fb442d3b773)

#### 

[​](https://www.recraft.ai/docs/recraft-studio/mockups/how-to-create-a-mockup#3-convert-an-existing-image-to-a-mockup)

3\. Convert an existing image to a mockup

You can also convert any photorealistic image (e.g., a stock photo of a product) into a mockup:

1.  Place the image onto the canvas.
2.  Select the image and in the right panel, click **Convert to mockup**.
3.  The image will be converted into a mockup frame.

![Screenshot 2026 06 04 At 01 52 28](https://mintcdn.com/recraft/0w-OP7I9SRQQy24t/images/Screenshot-2026-06-04-at-01.52.28.png?w=2500&fit=max&auto=format&n=0w-OP7I9SRQQy24t&q=85&s=831cd99cb2bc837c0d7b6dca2704d8db)

This method works best with any suitable object in an image, such as T-shirts, cups, packaging, notebooks, etc. You can also generate a product photo in a photorealistic style and convert it the same way.

[​](https://www.recraft.ai/docs/recraft-studio/mockups/how-to-create-a-mockup#enhance-realism)

Enhance realism
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

For mockups with flat surfaces — such as packaging or devices — you may want to refine how the design sits on the object, so it follows the correct perspective or fits precisely onto a screen. Use the **Enhance realism** function to blend your design more naturally into the mockup. It uses the Nano Banana 2 model and costs **11 credits**. This step is optional — depending on the mockup, you may or may not need it.

#### 

[​](https://www.recraft.ai/docs/recraft-studio/mockups/how-to-create-a-mockup#)

[Outpainting](https://www.recraft.ai/docs/recraft-studio/frames/outpainting)
[Applying your design to the mockup](https://www.recraft.ai/docs/recraft-studio/mockups/applying-your-design-to-a-mockup)

⌘I

Assistant

Responses are generated using AI and may contain mistakes.

# Remix - Recraft

> Documentation Index
> -------------------
> 
> Fetch the complete documentation index at: [/docs/llms.txt](https://www.recraft.ai/docs/llms.txt)
> 
> Use this file to discover all available pages before exploring further.

[Skip to main content](https://www.recraft.ai/docs/recraft-studio/image-editing/remix#content-area)

Remix generates new versions of an image while keeping the overall concept intact. Each remix introduces slight differences in elements like character appearance, object position, or scene composition. Remix the image by adjusting the description and similarity strength. Start with an image, rewrite the prompt (e.g., ‘cat’ to ‘dog’), and set how closely the new image should match the original. The Remix function does not use a prompt. Instead, it uses the visual content of the original image to generate alternatives in different aspect ratios. **How to use Remix**:

1.  Select an existing image on the canvas.
2.  Click on the **Remix image** in the context panel.
    
    ![Image](https://mintcdn.com/recraft/RPmRUgr6M3jQk2x1/images/image-27.png?w=2500&fit=max&auto=format&n=RPmRUgr6M3jQk2x1&q=85&s=a91751aebeaa79649d0aaf94a42e1dfb)
    
3.  **Adjust similarity to the original**  
    Use the slider at the top to control how closely the new image should match the original. **Select the model**  
    Under the _Model_ section, choose the generation model.

*   Here, **V4** is selected. **Choose a style**  
    In the _Style_ section, you can apply a predefined style to the image.
*   Currently, **No styles** is selected.

![Image](https://mintcdn.com/recraft/RPmRUgr6M3jQk2x1/images/image-28.png?w=2500&fit=max&auto=format&n=RPmRUgr6M3jQk2x1&q=85&s=ed368b43866e24c00a51056456b63908)

4.  Click **Generate** to produce a set of new outputs based on the selected image.

[Raster effects](https://www.recraft.ai/docs/recraft-studio/image-editing/raster-effects)
[How to crop an image](https://www.recraft.ai/docs/recraft-studio/image-editing/how-to-crop-an-image)

# Background tools - Recraft

> Documentation Index
> -------------------
> 
> Fetch the complete documentation index at: [/docs/llms.txt](https://www.recraft.ai/docs/llms.txt)
> 
> Use this file to discover all available pages before exploring further.

[Skip to main content](https://www.recraft.ai/docs/recraft-studio/image-editing/background-tools#content-area)

[​](https://www.recraft.ai/docs/recraft-studio/image-editing/background-tools#remove-background)

Remove background
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Recraft Studio’s Remove background tool is especially tuned for AI-generated images, making it more effective than the background removal features found in most other AI image generators. You can remove the background from any image with one click, creating a transparent version for compositing or mockups. To remove a background, select the image and click **Remove background** in the context panel. The background will be deleted, leaving only the subject. This is especially useful for preparing product overlays or isolating graphics. Remove background functionality works with images with resolution of 1024 by the smaller side. For images with large resolution there might be some artifacts on the border of the image. **Note**: When using Remove background on large images, Recraft automatically downscales the image before applying edits, which can result in a noticeable loss of quality in the final output.

[​](https://www.recraft.ai/docs/recraft-studio/image-editing/background-tools#change-background)

Change background
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

**How to change the background of an image**:

1.  Select a generated or uploaded image.
2.  Select the image, then click **Change background** in the context panel.
3.  Wait for the background area to be masked.
4.  Enter a new prompt for the background in the prompt panel, then click the **generate button**.
5.  Your image with new backgrond will appear on the canvas as a new image.

[How to crop an image](https://www.recraft.ai/docs/recraft-studio/image-editing/how-to-crop-an-image)
[About importing](https://www.recraft.ai/docs/recraft-studio/importing/about-importing)

⌘I

Responses are generated using AI and may contain mistakes.

# Raster effects - Recraft

> Documentation Index
> -------------------
> 
> Fetch the complete documentation index at: [/docs/llms.txt](https://www.recraft.ai/docs/llms.txt)
> 
> Use this file to discover all available pages before exploring further.

[Skip to main content](https://www.recraft.ai/docs/recraft-studio/image-editing/raster-effects#content-area)

Recraft Studio effects let you add visual treatments to any **raster image** on the canvas, such as illustrations, photos, or painted textures. These effects do not apply to vector images. You can combine multiple effects, reorder them, or remove them at any time. Effects are non-destructive; you can remove them without modifying the original image.

[​](https://www.recraft.ai/docs/recraft-studio/image-editing/raster-effects#accessing-raster-effects)

Accessing raster effects
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Raster effects are accessed through the **Adjust colors** control in the context panel. To open raster effects:

1.  Select a **raster image** on the canvas.
2.  In the right sidebar (context panel), click **Adjust colors**.
3.  Click **+** in the **Effects** section to add an effect, such as **Blur**, **Drop Shadow**, or **Stroke**.

The Effects section is available only when a raster image is selected.

[​](https://www.recraft.ai/docs/recraft-studio/image-editing/raster-effects#drop-shadow)

Drop shadow
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Drop shadow adds depth by placing a soft shadow behind your image. To add a drop shadow:

1.  Select a raster image on the canvas.
2.  In the right sidebar, open the **Effects** section and choose **Drop Shadow**.
3.  Adjust the available controls:
    *   **Position (X, Y):** Offsets the shadow horizontally and vertically
    *   **Blur:** Controls how soft or sharp the shadow edge appears
    *   **Color:** Sets the shadow color (use darker tones for natural shadows)

Tip: Drop shadow also works with images with transparent backgrounds.

[​](https://www.recraft.ai/docs/recraft-studio/image-editing/raster-effects#stroke)

Stroke
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Stroke adds an outline around the frame of your raster image. To add a stroke:

1.  Select a raster image.
2.  In **Effects**, choose **Stroke**.
3.  Customize your outline using:
    *   **Weight:** Controls the thickness of the outline
    *   **Color:** Sets the outline color
    *   **Position:**
        *   **Inside** – stroke sits just inside the image boundary
        *   **Outside** – stroke sits outside the image boundary
        *   **Center** – stroke is placed half inside, half outside the boundary

[​](https://www.recraft.ai/docs/recraft-studio/image-editing/raster-effects#blur)

Blur
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Blur softens the entire image for atmospheric or stylistic effects. To apply a blur:

1.  Select a raster image.
2.  In **Effects**, choose **Blur**.
3.  Adjust the **Strength** slider to increase or decrease the blur intensity.

Blur is frequently used to create depth, soften textures, or reduce detail behind foreground elements.

[​](https://www.recraft.ai/docs/recraft-studio/image-editing/raster-effects#removing-an-effect)

Removing an effect
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Each effect added appears as an entry under **Effects** in the right sidebar. Click **–** next to any effect to remove it. Removing an effect immediately resets all of its settings to default.

[Manual editing tools](https://www.recraft.ai/docs/recraft-studio/image-editing/manual-editing-tools)
[Remix](https://www.recraft.ai/docs/recraft-studio/image-editing/remix)

⌘I

Assistant

Responses are generated using AI and may contain mistakes.

# Manual editing tools - Recraft

> Documentation Index
> -------------------
> 
> Fetch the complete documentation index at: [/docs/llms.txt](https://www.recraft.ai/docs/llms.txt)
> 
> Use this file to discover all available pages before exploring further.

[Skip to main content](https://www.recraft.ai/docs/recraft-studio/image-editing/manual-editing-tools#content-area)

**Manual selection tools** Recraft Studio provides several selection and modification tools for precise manual edits, such as the **Lasso**, **Brush**, **Area selector**, **Magic wand**, **Eraser**, and **Cut** tools. These allow fine control over what parts of an image are affected when applying edits, regenerations, or style changes. For detailed descriptions and usage of each tool, go to [Selection tools](https://www.recraft.ai/docs/recraft-studio/work-area/selection-tools)
.

[​](https://www.recraft.ai/docs/recraft-studio/image-editing/manual-editing-tools#edit-area)

Edit area
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

You can manually select and edit an image or design using the Edit area feature. To activate it, select an image on the canvas, then click **Edit area** in the context panel that appears at the right of the canvas. This will open a panel where you can choose the Lasso, Brush, Area, and Wand tools. To exit these selection tools, click **Edit area** again.

[​](https://www.recraft.ai/docs/recraft-studio/image-editing/manual-editing-tools#duplicate-an-image)

Duplicate an image
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

There are multiple ways to duplicate an image:

*   Use the copy-paste function: Cmd/Ctrl+C and Cmd/Ctrl+V
*   Hold Option on Mac and Alt on other OS, then click and drag the new image
*   Right-click the image and select **Duplicate**

[Editing images with natural language](https://www.recraft.ai/docs/recraft-studio/image-editing/editing-images-with-natural-language)
[Raster effects](https://www.recraft.ai/docs/recraft-studio/image-editing/raster-effects)

⌘I

# How To Generate A Video - Recraft

> Documentation Index
> -------------------
> 
> Fetch the complete documentation index at: [/docs/llms.txt](https://www.recraft.ai/docs/llms.txt)
> 
> Use this file to discover all available pages before exploring further.

[Skip to main content](https://www.recraft.ai/docs/recraft-studio/video-generation/how-to-generate-a-video#content-area)

[​](https://www.recraft.ai/docs/recraft-studio/video-generation/how-to-generate-a-video#overview)

Overview
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Recraft supports video generation powered by a curated selection of leading AI video models. Users can generate videos from text prompts or use existing images as starting frames — all within the same canvas workflow used for image generation. Video generation is available on **Pro plans** (new Pro plan, and legacy Pro 4K / Pro 8K plans) and **Team plans (all)**. As of now, the video is accessible on Desktop and Android, with iOS availability rolling out soon.

[​](https://www.recraft.ai/docs/recraft-studio/video-generation/how-to-generate-a-video#how-to-access-video-generation)

How to Access Video Generation
=========================================================================================================================================================

1.  Open the chat prompt panel.
2.  Click the “Image” control and switch to “Video.”
3.  Now you can select a particular video model in the models selector
4.  Type your prompt and generate a video

[​](https://www.recraft.ai/docs/recraft-studio/video-generation/how-to-generate-a-video#generation-modes)

Generation Modes
=============================================================================================================================

[​](https://www.recraft.ai/docs/recraft-studio/video-generation/how-to-generate-a-video#text-to-video)

Text-to-Video
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Describe a scene, action, or concept in the prompt, and the selected video model will generate a video clip from scratch. This works similarly to text-to-image generation — the more specific and descriptive the prompt, the better the result.

[​](https://www.recraft.ai/docs/recraft-studio/video-generation/how-to-generate-a-video#image-to-video)

Image-to-Video
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

To create a video using images, you can simply select an image(s) on the canvas or upload one using the attachment option in the prompt panel (paperclip icon). Some models support the **first frame** and the **last frame** of the video. This is useful for animating a specific composition, maintaining visual consistency with existing assets, or extending a still image into motion.

[​](https://www.recraft.ai/docs/recraft-studio/video-generation/how-to-generate-a-video#available-models)

Available Models
=============================================================================================================================

Recraft offers a range of video models, each with different strengths in quality, speed, and style.

| Model | Variants |
| --- | --- |
| Google Veo 3.1 | Standard, Fast |
| Google Veo 3 | Standard, Fast |
| Google Veo 2 | Standard |
| OpenAI Sora 2 | Standard, Pro |
| Luma Ray 2 | Standard, Flash |
| Kling 3 | Pro, Standard, Omni Pro, Omni Standard |
| Kling 2.6 | Pro |
| Kling 2.5 | Turbo |
| Kling 2.1 | Master |
| MiniMax Hailuo 2.3 | Pro, Standard |
| MiniMax Hailuo 02 | Pro, Standard |
| Wan 2.6 | Standard |
| Wan 2.5 | Preview |
| Wan 2.2 | A14B |
| ByteDance Seedance 1.5 | Standard |
| PixVerse 5.5 | Standard |
| Grok Imagine Video | Standard |

> **Note:** Model availability may change as new models are added and existing ones are updated. The credit cost varies by model and generation settings (resolution, duration, audio). See the in-app credit display for current pricing.

[​](https://www.recraft.ai/docs/recraft-studio/video-generation/how-to-generate-a-video#working-with-generated-videos)

Working with Generated Videos
=======================================================================================================================================================

Generated videos appear as **video layers** on the canvas, just like images.

*   **Play** the video directly on the canvas.
*   **Download** by right-clicking the video layer and selecting **Download** from the context menu.
*   **Reposition and resize** the video layer on the canvas alongside other assets

When generating or editing a video in Recraft Studio, you can interact with the project directly on the canvas. **Tip:** When interacting with a public project, your cursor, along with your username, will be visible to others.

[​](https://www.recraft.ai/docs/recraft-studio/video-generation/how-to-generate-a-video#plan-requirements)

Plan Requirements
===============================================================================================================================

Video generation is available on the following plans:

*   **Any Pro plan** (new)
*   **Legacy Pro 4K** and **Pro 8K** plans
*   **Any Team plan** (legacy and new)

Video generation is not available on Basic or Free plans as well as on legacy Pro 1k plan.

[Extract prompt](https://www.recraft.ai/docs/recraft-studio/image-generation/working-with-text-and-prompts/extract-prompt)
[Video Prompts](https://www.recraft.ai/docs/recraft-studio/video-generation/video-prompts)

⌘I

Assistant

Responses are generated using AI and may contain mistakes.

# Editing images with natural language - Recraft

> Documentation Index
> -------------------
> 
> Fetch the complete documentation index at: [/docs/llms.txt](https://www.recraft.ai/docs/llms.txt)
> 
> Use this file to discover all available pages before exploring further.

[Skip to main content](https://www.recraft.ai/docs/recraft-studio/image-editing/editing-images-with-natural-language#content-area)

Recraft Studio supports targeted image editing using integrated external models **Google Nano Banana**, **OpenAI GPT‑4o**, **Seedream**, **Flux Kontext**, and **Qwen-Image** that respond to natural language prompts and optional reference images. These models are built directly into the Recraft interface, so you can make precise edits without switching platforms or starting from scratch. Natural language editing allows you to modify specific aspects of an image (like clothing, background, or facial expression) while preserving the overall structure and style. Only the elements described in your prompt are changed; everything else remains intact.

[​](https://www.recraft.ai/docs/recraft-studio/image-editing/editing-images-with-natural-language#use-cases)

Use cases
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

*   Make small adjustments, such as changing clothing, background elements, or facial features
*   Refine visual details without regenerating the entire image
*   Maintain stylistic or character consistency across multiple images
*   Add, remove, or modify specific objects within a scene
*   Adjust visual elements like lighting, color palette, or seasonal context
*   Update product features or character traits while keeping composition intact
*   Apply a consistent style or mood using reference images

[​](https://www.recraft.ai/docs/recraft-studio/image-editing/editing-images-with-natural-language#how-to-edit-an-image-with-natural-language-prompts)

How to edit an image with natural language prompts
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

1.  Open a project and upload or generate the image you want to modify.
2.  Select the image on the canvas.
3.  In the prompt panel, select a model:
    *   **Nano Banana** (normal, Pro, Pro 4K)
    *   **Seedream V4**
    *   **GPT‑4o** (Low, Medium, or High quality)
    *   **Flux Kontext** (Pro or Max quality)
    *   **Qwen-Image**
4.  Enter a prompt describing the change (e.g., _“make the jacket red”_ or _“change background to nighttime”_).
5.  (Optional) Click the **paper clip icon** within the prompt panel to attach reference images:
    *   Up to **9 images** for GPT‑4o, Nano Banana, and Seedream
    *   **1 image** for Flux Kontext and Qwen-Image Reference images allow the model to incorporate visual elements like style, character, pose, or layout into the output. In your prompt, describe what you want to borrow from each image and how you’d like them composed.
6.  Click the **generate button** to apply the edit.
7.  You can repeat the process as needed. Each new edit builds on the previous result without requiring a full regeneration.

[​](https://www.recraft.ai/docs/recraft-studio/image-editing/editing-images-with-natural-language#supported-models)

Supported models
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Currently, the reference image feature is supported only by select external models. You can manually choose the model, or GPT‑4o Medium will be used by default when a reference image is attached. Recraft standard image generation is included in the table below for reference.

| Model | Credits |
| --- | --- |
| Recraft raster image generation | 1 credits |
| Recraft vector image generation | 2 credits |
| Flux Kontext Pro | 2 credits |
| Flux Kontext Max | 4 credits |
| GPT-4o Low | 1 credit |
| GPT-4o Medium | 6 credits |
| GPT-4o High | 24 credits |
| Nano Banana | 2 credits |
| Nano Banana Pro | 15 credits |
| Nano Banana Pro 4K | 30 credits |
| Seedream V4 | 2 credits |
| Qwen-Image | 2 credits |

[​](https://www.recraft.ai/docs/recraft-studio/image-editing/editing-images-with-natural-language#notes-on-external-models)

Notes on external models
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Each external model has its own supported aspect ratios. For example, GPT‑4o supports only 1:1, 3:2, and 2:3 formats. If your original image uses an unsupported aspect ratio (e.g., 16:9), the output will default to the closest supported format. The credit cost for using external models depends on each model’s API pricing.

[Video Prompts](https://www.recraft.ai/docs/recraft-studio/video-generation/video-prompts)
[Manual editing tools](https://www.recraft.ai/docs/recraft-studio/image-editing/manual-editing-tools)

⌘I

Assistant

Responses are generated using AI and may contain mistakes.

# Curated styles - Recraft

> Documentation Index
> -------------------
> 
> Fetch the complete documentation index at: [/docs/llms.txt](https://www.recraft.ai/docs/llms.txt)
> 
> Use this file to discover all available pages before exploring further.

[Skip to main content](https://www.recraft.ai/docs/recraft-studio/styles/curated-styles#content-area)

To apply a curated style, click the **Styles button** in the prompt panel before generating your image and make sure the **Curated tab** is selected. You can browse styles created and selected by the Recraft team, apply styles you’ve saved, or select styles that have been shared with you. If you frequently use a particular style, click the **bookmark icon** in the upper right corner of the style panel. This adds the style to your library, making it easier to access in future projects.

[Overview](https://www.recraft.ai/docs/recraft-studio/styles/overview)
[How to create a custom style](https://www.recraft.ai/docs/recraft-studio/styles/custom-styles/how-to-create-a-custom-style)

# Templates - Recraft

> Documentation Index
> -------------------
> 
> Fetch the complete documentation index at: [/docs/llms.txt](https://www.recraft.ai/docs/llms.txt)
> 
> Use this file to discover all available pages before exploring further.

[Skip to main content](https://www.recraft.ai/docs/recraft-studio/templates#content-area)

Templates help you generate structured visuals faster by starting from curated examples or applying predefined transformations to an existing image. The **Templates** panel contains two modes:

*   **Collections**: pre-generated prompt + style combinations
*   **Editing templates**: structured transformations applied to your uploaded image

Both are accessed from the same place.

[​](https://www.recraft.ai/docs/recraft-studio/templates#how-to-access-templates)

How to access Templates
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Templates are available from the top navigation bar inside Recraft Studio.

1.  Open any project.
2.  In the top toolbar, click **Templates** (next to History and Help).
3.  The Templates panel will open.
4.  Choose between:
    *   **Collections**
    *   **Editing templates**

You can switch between the two tabs at any time.

[​](https://www.recraft.ai/docs/recraft-studio/templates#collections)

Collections
====================================================================================

Collections are pre-generated visual examples organized by outcome type. They help you start from a proven visual direction instead of writing a prompt from scratch. Examples include:

*   Lifestyle photo
*   Vector illustration
*   Product mockup
*   Modern minimal logo
*   Hand-drawn illustration
*   Vector set
*   Concept art
*   Web design

(Available categories may change over time.) Each Collection represents:

*   A curated prompt
*   A selected style
*   A structured visual outcome

They show you what is possible before you generate anything.

[​](https://www.recraft.ai/docs/recraft-studio/templates#how-to-use-collections)

How to use Collections
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

1.  Open **Templates → Collections**.
2.  Click a category (for example, _Product mockup_).
3.  Select one of the example images.

You will see two options:

### 

[​](https://www.recraft.ai/docs/recraft-studio/templates#use-prompt)

Use prompt

Generates a new image using the same underlying prompt + style logic. The result will be similar in structure and aesthetic, but not identical.

### 

[​](https://www.recraft.ai/docs/recraft-studio/templates#use-as-reference)

Use as reference

Attaches the selected example to your prompt as a visual reference. You can then:

*   Write your own prompt
*   Combine it with the reference
*   Generate a new image influenced by that layout or style

[​](https://www.recraft.ai/docs/recraft-studio/templates#when-to-use-collections)

When to use Collections
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Use Collections when:

*   You want a fast starting point
*   You know the type of visual you need, but not the exact prompt
*   You want structured results (mockups, posters, logos, etc.)
*   You want inspiration with production-ready direction

[​](https://www.recraft.ai/docs/recraft-studio/templates#editing-templates)

Editing templates
================================================================================================

Editing templates transform an existing image using predefined visual logic. Unlike Collections, which generate new images, Editing templates modify your uploaded image. They apply structured transformations behind the scenes, so you don’t need to engineer the prompt manually.

[​](https://www.recraft.ai/docs/recraft-studio/templates#how-to-use-editing-templates)

How to use Editing templates
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

1.  Open **Templates → Editing templates**.
2.  Select a template (for example, _Product photoshoot_).
3.  Click **Upload your image**.
4.  Choose a visual direction (if the template offers multiple looks).
5.  Click **Run the template**.

The system:

*   Preserves your subject
*   Applies the selected transformation
*   Generates a new edited version

[​](https://www.recraft.ai/docs/recraft-studio/templates#types-of-editing-templates)

Types of Editing templates
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Available templates may change, but generally include transformations such as:

*   **Product photoshoot**: convert a product image into a studio-quality visual
*   **Sketch to photo**: turn a drawing into a realistic render
*   **Angles**: generate alternative perspectives of the same object
*   **Apply texture**: change surface material or visual finish
*   **Portrait transformations**: apply editorial lighting or stylized looks
*   **Graphic treatments**: create themed or layout-based variations

Each template is optimized for a specific type of transformation.

[​](https://www.recraft.ai/docs/recraft-studio/templates#when-to-use-editing-templates)

When to use Editing templates
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Use Editing templates when:

*   You already have a base image
*   You want structured visual transformation
*   You need consistent variations
*   You want faster results without iterative prompting

Editing templates provide predictable, production-ready transformations while keeping your original subject intact.

[Community](https://www.recraft.ai/docs/recraft-studio/libraries/community)
[How to export an image](https://www.recraft.ai/docs/recraft-studio/exporting-and-sharing/how-to-export-an-image)

⌘I

Assistant

Responses are generated using AI and may contain mistakes.

# Seamless patterns - Recraft

> Documentation Index

>

[Skip to main content](https://www.recraft.ai/docs/recraft-studio/styles/seamless-patterns#content-area)

Recraft Studio supports seamless pattern generation for both raster and vector formats. These patterns are tileable by nature, meaning they can be repeated across large areas without noticeable edges. Seamless patterns are commonly used for website backgrounds, social media graphics, presentation visuals, textile and surface design, product packaging, and branding materials.

[​](https://www.recraft.ai/docs/recraft-studio/styles/seamless-patterns#how-to-create-a-seamless-pattern)

How to create a seamless pattern
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

1.  Click the **Style button** in the prompt panel to open the **Styles** panel.  
    a. For a raster-based pattern, scroll down to **Illustration** and select **Seamless Digital**.  
    b. For a scalable vector pattern, scroll down to **Vector art** and select **Seamless Vector**.
2.  In the prompt field, describe the pattern you want to generate. You can also adjust visual complexity using the **Specify Artistry level** slider.  
    a. After generation, you can use editing tools to adjust colors, shapes, layout, or iterate on variations.
3.  Export your pattern to PNG, JPEG, TIFF (CMYK), SVG, PDF, or Lottie.

[Sharing a style](https://www.recraft.ai/docs/recraft-studio/styles/sharing-a-style)
[Introduction to frames](https://www.recraft.ai/docs/recraft-studio/frames/introduction-to-frames)

⌘I

Assistant

Responses are generated using AI and may contain mistakes.

# Sharing a style - Recraft

> Documentation Index
> -------------------
> 
> Fetch the complete documentation index at: [/docs/llms.txt](https://www.recraft.ai/docs/llms.txt)
> 
> Use this file to discover all available pages before exploring further.

[Skip to main content](https://www.recraft.ai/docs/recraft-studio/styles/sharing-a-style#content-area)

There are two ways to browse styles for sharing in Recraft Studio:

*   From within the **canvas**, using the Styles panel
*   On the standalone styles page: [recraft.ai/styles](https://www.recraft.ai/styles)
    

You can share styles from either location, but the sharing options differ slightly depending on whether the style is public or one you’ve created yourself.

[​](https://www.recraft.ai/docs/recraft-studio/styles/sharing-a-style#how-to-share-a-style)

How to share a style
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

1.  Open the **Styles panel** (from the prompt panel or styles page).
2.  Click on the style you want to share.
3.  If it’s a public style (e.g. from the Feed), click the **three-dot menu** near the top of the page and choose:
    *   **Copy link to style** – generates a public URL you can share with anyone
    *   **Copy style ID** – for use with the Recraft API or developer workflows
4.  If it’s a **style you’ve created**, click **Share style**. This opens a dialog similar to project sharing, where you can invite collaborators by email and manage their access.

Anyone with an active Recraft account can view and apply a shared style in their own projects. You can find:

*   Styles **shared with you** in the **Shared** tab of the Styles panel
*   Styles **you’ve shared** by revisiting the original style and checking the sharing settings

[How to delete a custom style](https://www.recraft.ai/docs/recraft-studio/styles/custom-styles/how-to-delete-a-custom-style)
[Seamless patterns](https://www.recraft.ai/docs/recraft-studio/styles/seamless-patterns)

⌘I

Assistant

Responses are generated using AI and may contain mistakes.

-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Text
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Add and format editable text layers using Google Fonts.

[​](https://www.recraft.ai/docs/recraft-studio/work-area/canvas-tools#brush)

Brush
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Freehand tool with adjustable size. Useful for rough markup, masking, or collaborative notes. Adjust size with bracket keys **\[** and **\]**.
